{"parentUuid":"12eb917a-2fea-42ec-aee3-3cf1155509a5","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"67fcde4a-7483-4526-a2da-9ae9514890c8","agentId":"adc2b12a4da32c962","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01P7A6NhaXHz7aoXp6uoZbVJ","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Review Loop Pattern Reference\n     2→\n     3→Canonical reference for the review loop pattern used across all Wazir pipeline phases. Skills and workflows link to this document rather than embedding loop logic inline.\n     4→\n     5→---\n     6→\n     7→## Core Principle: Producer-Reviewer Separation\n     8→\n     9→The producer skill (clarifier, planner, designer, etc.) **emits** an artifact and calls for review. The **reviewer role** owns the review loop. The producer receives findings and resolves them. No role reviews its own output.\n    10→\n    11→```\n    12→Producer emits artifact\n    13→  -> Reviewer runs review loop (N passes, Codex if available)\n    14→  -> Findings returned to producer\n    15→  -> Producer fixes and resubmits\n    16→  -> Loop until all passes exhausted or cap reached\n    17→  -> Escalate to user if cap exceeded\n    18→```\n    19→\n    20→When Codex is available, the reviewer role delegates to `codex review` as a secondary input while maintaining its own independent primary verdict.\n    21→\n    22→---\n    23→\n    24→## Per-Task Review vs Final Review\n    25→\n    26→These are two structurally different constructs:\n    27→\n    28→| | Per-Task Review | Final Review |\n    29→|---|---|---|\n    30→| **When** | During execution, after each task | After all execution + verification complete |\n    31→| **Dimensions** | 5 task-execution dims (correctness, tests, wiring, drift, quality) | 9 scored dims (correctness, completeness, wiring, verification, drift, quality, documentation, intent alignment, scope coverage) |\n    32→| **Scope** | Single task's uncommitted changes | Entire implementation vs spec/plan |\n    33→| **Output** | Pass/fix loop, no score | Scored verdict (0-90), PASS/FAIL |\n    34→| **Workflow** | Inline in execution flow | `workflows/review.md` |\n    35→| **Skill** | `wz:reviewer` in `task-review` mode | `wz:reviewer` in `final` mode |\n    36→| **Log filename** | `<phase>-task-<NNN>-review-pass-<N>.md` | `final-review.md` |\n    37→\n    38→---\n    39→\n    40→## Standalone Mode\n    41→\n    42→When no `.wazir/runs/latest/` directory exists (standalone skill invocation outside a pipeline run):\n    43→\n    44→1. **Review loops still run** -- the review logic is embedded in the skill, not dependent on run state.\n    45→2. **Artifact location** -- artifacts live in `docs/plans/`. This is the canonical standalone artifact path.\n    46→3. **Review log location** -- review logs go alongside the artifact: `docs/plans/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-review-pass-<N>.md`. No temp dir.\n    47→4. **Loop cap is SKIPPED entirely** -- no `wazir capture loop-check` call. The loop runs for exactly `pass_counts[depth]` passes (3/5/7) and stops. No cap guard, no fallback constant.\n    48→5. **`wazir capture loop-check`** -- not invoked in standalone mode. The standalone detection happens before the cap guard call.\n    49→\n    50→Detection logic:\n    51→\n    52→```\n    53→if .wazir/runs/latest/ exists:\n    54→  run_mode = \"pipeline\"\n    55→  log_dir = .wazir/runs/latest/reviews/\n    56→  cap_guard = wazir capture loop-check (full guard)\n    57→else:\n    58→  run_mode = \"standalone\"\n    59→  artifact_dir = docs/plans/\n    60→  log_dir = docs/plans/  (alongside artifact)\n    61→  cap_guard = none (depth pass count is the only limit)\n    62→```\n    63→\n    64→---\n    65→\n    66→## Review Loop Pseudocode\n    67→\n    68→```\n    69→review_loop(artifact_path, phase, dimensions[], depth, config, options={}):\n    70→\n    71→  # options.mode      -- explicit review mode (required)\n    72→  # options.task_id   -- task identifier for task-scoped reviews (optional)\n    73→\n    74→  # Standalone detection\n    75→  run_mode = detect_run_mode()  # \"pipeline\" or \"standalone\"\n    76→\n    77→  # Fixed pass counts -- no extension\n    78→  pass_counts = { quick: 3, standard: 5, deep: 7 }\n    79→  total_passes = pass_counts[depth]\n    80→\n    81→  # Depth-aware dimension subsets (coverage contract)\n    82→  depth_dimensions = {\n    83→    quick:    dimensions[0:3],     # first 3 dimensions only\n    84→    standard: dimensions[0:5],     # first 5\n    85→    deep:     dimensions,          # all available\n    86→  }\n    87→  active_dims = depth_dimensions[depth]\n    88→\n    89→  codex_available = check_codex()  # which codex && codex --version\n    90→\n    91→  for pass_number in 0..total_passes-1:\n    92→\n    93→    # --- Cap guard check (pipeline mode only, before each pass) ---\n    94→    if run_mode == \"pipeline\":\n    95→      loop_check_args = \"--run <run-id> --phase <phase> --loop-count <pass_number+1>\"\n    96→      if options.task_id:\n    97→        loop_check_args += \" --task-id <task_id>\"\n    98→      wazir capture loop-check $loop_check_args\n    99→      # loop-check wraps: event capture + evaluateLoopCapGuard\n   100→      # If loop_cap_guard fires (exit 43), stop immediately:\n   101→      if last_exit_code == 43:\n   102→        log(\"Loop cap reached for phase: <phase>. Escalating to user.\")\n   103→        escalate_to_user(evidence_gathered_so_far)\n   104→        return { pass_count: pass_number, escalated: true }\n   105→    # Standalone mode: no cap guard. Loop runs for total_passes and stops.\n   106→\n   107→    dimension = active_dims[pass_number % len(active_dims)]\n   108→\n   109→    # --- Primary review (reviewer role, not producer) ---\n   110→    # Mode is always explicit -- passed by caller via options.mode\n   111→    findings = self_review(artifact_path, focus=dimension, mode=options.mode)\n   112→\n   113→    # --- Secondary review (Codex, if available) ---\n   114→    if codex_available:\n   115→      codex_exit_code, codex_output = run_codex_review(artifact_path, dimension)\n   116→      if codex_exit_code != 0:\n   117→        # Codex failed -- log error, fall back to self-review for this pass\n   118→        log_error(\"Codex exited \" + codex_exit_code + \": \" + codex_output.stderr)\n   119→        mark_pass_codex_unavailable(pass_number)\n   120→        # Do NOT treat Codex failure as clean. Self-review findings stand alone.\n   121→      else:\n   122→        codex_findings = parse(codex_output.stdout)\n   123→        merge(findings, codex_findings, preserve_attribution=true)\n   124→\n   125→    # --- Log the review pass ---\n   126→    if run_mode == \"pipeline\":\n   127→      if options.task_id:\n   128→        log_path = .wazir/runs/latest/reviews/<phase>-task-<task_id>-review-pass-<N>.md\n   129→      else:\n   130→        log_path = .wazir/runs/latest/reviews/<phase>-review-pass-<N>.md\n   131→      log(pass_number+1, dimension, findings) -> log_path\n   132→    else:\n   133→      log_path = docs/plans/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-review-pass-<N>.md\n   134→      log(pass_number+1, dimension, findings) -> log_path\n   135→\n   136→    if findings.has_issues:\n   137→      # --- Fix and re-submit (MANDATORY) ---\n   138→      # The producer MUST fix findings and the reviewer MUST re-review.\n   139→      # \"Fix and continue without re-review\" is EXPLICITLY PROHIBITED.\n   140→      producer_fix(artifact_path, findings)\n   141→      # Continue to next pass -- the fix will be re-reviewed\n   142→\n   143→  # --- Post-loop: escalation if issues remain ---\n   144→  if remaining.has_issues:\n   145→    # Cap reached with unresolved findings. Present to user:\n   146→    # 1. Approve with known issues (Recommended if non-blocking)\n   147→    # 2. Fix manually and re-run\n   148→    # 3. Abort\n   149→    escalate_to_user(remaining, options=[\n   150→      \"approve-with-issues\",\n   151→      \"fix-manually-and-rerun\",\n   152→      \"abort\"\n   153→    ])\n   154→    # User decides. If approved, log \"user-approved-with-issues\" in final pass file.\n   155→\n   156→  return { pass_count: total_passes, issues_found, issues_fixed, remaining, attributions }\n   157→```\n   158→\n   159→Key properties of this pseudocode:\n   160→\n   161→1. **Fixed pass counts** -- Quick is exactly 3, standard exactly 5, deep exactly 7. No `max_passes = min_passes + 3`. No clean-streak early-exit. No extension.\n   162→2. **Task-scoped log filenames** -- `<phase>-task-<NNN>-review-pass-<N>.md` for per-task reviews, preventing log clobbering in parallel mode.\n   163→3. **Task-scoped loop cap keys** -- `--task-id` flag on `loop-check` so each task gets its own counter in `phase_loop_counts`.\n   164→4. **Explicit review mode** -- `options.mode` is always passed by the caller. No auto-detection.\n   165→5. **Codex error handling** -- non-zero exit is logged, pass marked `codex-unavailable`, self-review findings used alone. Never treated as clean.\n   166→6. **Standalone mode** -- uses `docs/plans/` for artifacts and logs. No temp dir. No cap guard at all.\n   167→\n   168→---\n   169→\n   170→## Codex Error Handling Contract\n   171→\n   172→```\n   173→run_codex_review(artifact_path, dimension):\n   174→  CODEX_MODEL = read_config('.wazir/state/config.json', '.multi_tool.codex.model') or \"gpt-5.4\"\n   175→\n   176→  if is_code_artifact:\n   177→    cmd = codex review -c model=\"$CODEX_MODEL\" --uncommitted --title \"...\" \"Review for [dimension]...\"\n   178→    # or: codex review -c model=\"$CODEX_MODEL\" --base <sha> for committed changes\n   179→  else:\n   180→    cmd = cat <artifact_path> | codex exec -c model=\"$CODEX_MODEL\" \"Review this [type] for [dimension]...\"\n   181→\n   182→  result = execute(cmd, timeout=120s, capture_stderr=true)\n   183→\n   184→  if result.exit_code != 0:\n   185→    return (result.exit_code, { stderr: result.stderr, stdout: \"\" })\n   186→    # Caller handles: log error, mark codex-unavailable, use self-review only\n   187→\n   188→  return (0, { stdout: result.stdout, stderr: result.stderr })\n   189→```\n   190→\n   191→Rules:\n   192→\n   193→- If Codex exits non-zero, log the full stderr.\n   194→- Mark the pass as `codex-unavailable` in the review log metadata.\n   195→- Fall back to self-review for that pass only. Do not skip the pass.\n   196→- Do not retry Codex on the same pass. If Codex fails on pass 2, pass 3 still tries Codex (transient failures recover).\n   197→- Never treat a Codex failure as a clean review pass.\n   198→\n   199→---\n   200→\n   201→## Codex Availability Probe\n   202→\n   203→Before any Codex call, verify availability once at loop start:\n   204→\n   205→```bash\n   206→which codex >/dev/null 2>&1 && codex --version >/dev/null 2>&1\n   207→```\n   208→\n   209→If the probe fails, set `codex_available = false` for the entire loop. Fall back to self-review only. Never error out.\n   210→\n   211→Per-invocation failures (Codex available but a single call fails) are handled separately by the error contract above.\n   212→\n   213→---\n   214→\n   215→## Codex Artifact-Scoped Review\n   216→\n   217→Never use `codex review` for non-code artifacts (specs, plans, designs). Instead, pipe the artifact content via stdin:\n   218→\n   219→```bash\n   220→CODEX_MODEL=$(jq -r '.multi_tool.codex.model // empty' .wazir/state/config.json 2>/dev/null)\n   221→CODEX_MODEL=${CODEX_MODEL:-gpt-5.4}\n   222→cat .wazir/runs/latest/clarified/spec-hardened.md | \\\n   223→  codex exec -c model=\"$CODEX_MODEL\" \"Review this specification for: [dimension]. Be specific, cite sections. Say CLEAN if no issues.\" \\\n   224→  2>&1 | tee .wazir/runs/latest/reviews/spec-challenge-review-pass-N.md\n   225→```\n   226→\n   227→For code artifacts, use `codex review -c model=\"$CODEX_MODEL\" --uncommitted` (or `--base` for committed changes). See the next section for details.\n   228→\n   229→---\n   230→\n   231→## Code Review Scoping\n   232→\n   233→**Rule: review BEFORE commit.**\n   234→\n   235→For each task during execution:\n   236→\n   237→1. Implement the task (changes are uncommitted).\n   238→2. Review the uncommitted changes using the **5 task-execution dimensions** (NOT the 9 final-review dimensions):\n   239→   ```bash\n   240→   CODEX_MODEL=$(jq -r '.multi_tool.codex.model // empty' .wazir/state/config.json 2>/dev/null)\n   241→CODEX_MODEL=${CODEX_MODEL:-gpt-5.4}\n   242→   codex review -c model=\"$CODEX_MODEL\" --uncommitted --title \"Task NNN: <summary>\" \\\n   243→     \"Review against acceptance criteria: <criteria>\" \\\n   244→     2>&1 | tee .wazir/runs/latest/reviews/execute-task-NNN-review-pass-N.md\n   245→   ```\n   246→3. Fix any findings (still uncommitted).\n   247→4. Re-review until all passes exhausted or cap reached.\n   248→5. **Only after review passes:** commit with conventional commit format.\n   249→\n   250→**If changes are already committed** (e.g., subagent workflow where the implementer subagent commits before review):\n   251→\n   252→```bash\n   253→# Capture the SHA before the task starts\n   254→PRE_TASK_SHA=$(git rev-parse HEAD)\n   255→\n   256→# ... subagent implements and commits ...\n   257→\n   258→# Review the committed changes against the pre-task baseline\n   259→CODEX_MODEL=$(jq -r '.multi_tool.codex.model // empty' .wazir/state/config.json 2>/dev/null)\n   260→CODEX_MODEL=${CODEX_MODEL:-gpt-5.4}\n   261→codex review -c model=\"$CODEX_MODEL\" --base $PRE_TASK_SHA --title \"Task NNN: <summary>\" \\\n   262→  \"Review against acceptance criteria: <criteria>\" \\\n   263→  2>&1 | tee .wazir/runs/latest/reviews/execute-task-NNN-review-pass-N.md\n   264→```\n   265→\n   266→---\n   267→\n   268→## Dimension Sets\n   269→\n   270→### Research Dimensions (5)\n   271→\n   272→1. **Coverage** -- all briefing topics researched\n   273→2. **Source quality** -- authoritative, current sources\n   274→3. **Relevance** -- research answers the actual questions\n   275→4. **Gaps** -- missing info that blocks later phases\n   276→5. **Contradictions** -- conflicting sources identified\n   277→\n   278→### Spec/Clarification Dimensions (5)\n   279→\n   280→1. **Completeness** -- all requirements covered\n   281→2. **Testability** -- each criterion verifiable\n   282→3. **Ambiguity** -- no dual-interpretation statements\n   283→4. **Assumptions** -- hidden assumptions explicit\n   284→5. **Scope creep** -- nothing beyond briefing\n   285→\n   286→### Design-Review Dimensions (5)\n   287→\n   288→Matches canonical `workflows/design-review.md`:\n   289→\n   290→1. **Spec coverage** -- does the design address every acceptance criterion with a visual component?\n   291→2. **Design-spec consistency** -- does the design introduce anything not in the spec? (scope creep check)\n   292→3. **Accessibility** -- color contrast ratios (WCAG 2.1 AA), focus states, touch target sizes (44x44px minimum)\n   293→4. **Visual consistency** -- design tokens form a coherent system, dark/light mode alignment\n   294→5. **Exported-code fidelity** -- do exported scaffolds match the designs? Mismatches are failures here, not implementation concerns.\n   295→\n   296→### Plan Dimensions (8)\n   297→\n   298→1. **Completeness** -- all design decisions mapped to tasks\n   299→2. **Ordering** -- dependencies correct, parallelizable identified\n   300→3. **Atomicity** -- each task fits one session\n   301→4. **Testability** -- concrete verification per task\n   302→5. **Edge cases** -- error paths covered\n   303→6. **Security** -- auth, injection, data exposure\n   304→7. **Integration** -- tasks connect end-to-end\n   305→8. **Input Coverage** -- every distinct item in the original input maps to at least one task. If `tasks < input items`, HIGH finding listing missing items\n   306→\n   307→### Task Execution Dimensions (5)\n   308→\n   309→Used for per-task review during execution:\n   310→\n   311→1. **Correctness** -- code matches spec\n   312→2. **Tests** -- real tests, not mocked/faked\n   313→3. **Wiring** -- all paths connected\n   314→4. **Drift** -- matches task spec\n   315→5. **Quality** -- naming, error handling\n   316→\n   317→### Final Review Dimensions (9)\n   318→\n   319→Used for `workflows/review.md` scored gate:\n   320→\n   321→1. **Correctness** -- does the code do what the spec says?\n   322→2. **Completeness** -- are all acceptance criteria met?\n   323→3. **Wiring** -- are all paths connected end-to-end?\n   324→4. **Verification** -- is there evidence (tests, type checks) for each claim?\n   325→5. **Drift** -- does the implementation match the approved plan?\n   326→6. **Quality** -- code style, naming, error handling, security\n   327→7. **Documentation** -- changelog entries, commit messages, comments\n   328→8. **Intent Alignment** -- does the implementation match what the user originally asked for, including mid-run corrections from `user-input-log.ndjson`? Compare against the RAW INPUT, not the spec. Score 0 if implementation contradicts a user correction.\n   329→9. **Scope Coverage** -- count distinct items in the original input vs items implemented. Flag missing items as HIGH. Score = (implemented / input items) * 10.\n   330→\n   331→The final review dimensions are the existing 9 from `skills/reviewer/SKILL.md`. `workflows/review.md` is not modified by this pattern.\n   332→\n   333→---\n   334→\n   335→## Per-Depth Coverage Contract\n   336→\n   337→| Depth | Research | Spec | Design-Review | Plan | Task Execution | Final Review |\n   338→|-------|----------|------|---------------|------|----------------|--------------|\n   339→| Quick | dims 1-3, 3 passes | dims 1-3, 3 passes | dims 1-3, 3 passes | dims 1-3, 3 passes | dims 1-3, 3 passes | always 9 dims, 1 pass |\n   340→| Standard | dims 1-5, 5 passes | dims 1-5, 5 passes | dims 1-5, 5 passes | dims 1-5, 5 passes | dims 1-5, 5 passes | always 9 dims, 1 pass |\n   341→| Deep | dims 1-5, 7 passes | dims 1-5, 7 passes | dims 1-5, 7 passes | dims 1-7, 7 passes | dims 1-5, 7 passes | always 9 dims, 1 pass |\n   342→\n   343→Pass counts are FIXED per depth. Quick = 3 passes, standard = 5 passes, deep = 7 passes. No extension. No early-exit. Final review is always a single scored pass across all 9 dimensions -- it is a gate, not a loop.\n   344→\n   345→---\n   346→\n   347→## Loop Cap Configuration\n   348→\n   349→The `workflow_policy` section of `run-config.yaml` (legacy: `phase_policy`) controls which workflows are enabled and sets an absolute safety ceiling per workflow. Only two fields exist: `enabled` and `loop_cap`. There is no `passes` field -- depth determines pass counts (3/5/7), not workflow policy.\n   350→\n   351→```yaml\n   352→workflow_policy:\n   353→  # Clarifier phase workflows\n   354→  discover:       { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   355→  clarify:        { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   356→  specify:        { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   357→  spec-challenge: { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   358→  author:         { enabled: false, loop_cap: 10 }\n   359→  design:         { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   360→  design-review:  { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   361→  plan:           { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   362→  plan-review:    { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   363→  # Executor phase workflows\n   364→  execute:        { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   365→  verify:         { enabled: true, loop_cap: 5 }\n   366→  review:         { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   367→  learn:          { enabled: true, loop_cap: 5 }\n   368→  prepare_next:   { enabled: true, loop_cap: 5 }\n   369→  run_audit:      { enabled: false, loop_cap: 10 }\n   370→```\n   371→\n   372→**`loop_cap`** is an absolute safety ceiling that prevents runaway loops regardless of depth. It is checked by `wazir capture loop-check` in pipeline mode. It is NOT the same as pass count (which is determined by depth: 3/5/7). Example: depth=deep gives 7 passes, but if `loop_cap: 5`, the cap guard fires at pass 5 and escalates. This is intentional -- the operator can constrain expensive phases.\n   373→\n   374→**Adaptive workflows** (`author`, `run_audit`) default to `enabled: false`. They are activated by explicit operator config or intent detection.\n   375→\n   376→**Post-run workflows** (`learn`, `prepare_next`) default to `enabled: true`. They run as part of the Final Review phase:\n   377→\n   378→- `learn` extracts durable learnings from review findings -- recurring findings become accepted learnings.\n   379→- `prepare_next` prepares context and handoff for the next run.\n   380→- `author` has a human approval gate, not an iterative review loop.\n   381→- `run_audit` is an on-demand standalone audit, not part of the main pipeline flow.\n   382→\n   383→---\n   384→\n   385→## Reviewer Mode Table\n   386→\n   387→The reviewer skill operates in different modes depending on the phase. **Mode is always explicit** -- the caller passes `--mode <mode>`. There is no auto-detection based on artifact availability.\n   388→\n   389→| Mode | Invoked during | Prerequisites | Dimensions | Output |\n   390→|------|---------------|---------------|------------|--------|\n   391→| `final` | After execution + verification | Completed task artifacts in `.wazir/runs/latest/artifacts/` | 9 final-review dims, scored 0-90 | Verdict: PASS/NEEDS FIXES/NEEDS REWORK/FAIL |\n   392→| `spec-challenge` | After specify | Draft spec artifact | 5 spec/clarification dims | Findings with severity, no score |\n   393→| `design-review` | After design approval | Design artifact, approved spec, accessibility guidelines | 5 design-review dims (canonical) | Findings with severity (blocking/advisory) |\n   394→| `plan-review` | After planning | Draft plan, approved spec, design artifact | 7 plan dims | Findings with severity, no score |\n   395→| `task-review` | During execution, per task | Uncommitted changes (or committed with known base SHA) | 5 task-execution dims | Pass/fail per task, no score |\n   396→| `research-review` | During discover | Research artifact | 5 research dims | Findings with severity, no score |\n   397→| `clarification-review` | During clarify | Clarification artifact | 5 spec/clarification dims | Findings with severity, no score |\n   398→\n   399→If `--mode` is not provided, the reviewer asks the user which review to run. Auto-detection based on artifact availability is NOT used -- it causes ambiguity in resumed/multi-phase runs where stale artifacts from prior phases exist.\n   400→\n   401→Each caller is responsible for passing the correct mode:\n   402→\n   403→- Clarifier passes `--mode clarification-review` after Phase 1A\n   404→- Discover workflow passes `--mode research-review` after research\n   405→- Specifier flow passes `--mode spec-challenge` after specify\n   406→- Brainstorming passes `--mode design-review` after user approval\n   407→- Writing-plans passes `--mode plan-review` after planning\n   408→- Executor passes `--mode task-review` for each task\n   409→- `/wazir` runner passes `--mode final` for the final review gate\n   410→\n   411→---\n   412→\n   413→## Codex Prompt Templates\n   414→\n   415→All Codex invocations read the model from config with a fallback:\n   416→\n   417→```bash\n   418→CODEX_MODEL=$(jq -r '.multi_tool.codex.model // empty' .wazir/state/config.json 2>/dev/null)\n   419→CODEX_MODEL=${CODEX_MODEL:-gpt-5.4}\n   420→```\n   421→\n   422→### Artifact Review (specs, plans, designs via stdin)\n   423→\n   424→Use this template with `codex exec` for non-code artifacts piped via stdin:\n   425→\n   426→```bash\n   427→cat <artifact_path> | codex exec -c model=\"$CODEX_MODEL\" \\\n   428→  \"You are reviewing a [ARTIFACT_TYPE] for the Wazir engineering OS.\n   429→Focus on [DIMENSION]: [dimension description].\n   430→Rules: cite specific sections, be actionable, say CLEAN if no issues.\n   431→Do NOT load or invoke any skills. Do NOT read the codebase.\n   432→Review ONLY the content provided via stdin.\"\n   433→```\n   434→\n   435→Replace `[ARTIFACT_TYPE]` with: `specification`, `implementation plan`, `design document`, `research brief`, or `clarification`.\n   436→Replace `[DIMENSION]` and `[dimension description]` with the current review pass dimension from the relevant dimension set above.\n   437→\n   438→### Code Review (diffs via --uncommitted or --base)\n   439→\n   440→Use this template with `codex review` for code changes:\n   441→\n   442→```bash\n   443→codex review -c model=\"$CODEX_MODEL\" --uncommitted --title \"Task NNN: <summary>\" \\\n   444→  \"Review the code changes for [DIMENSION]: [dimension description].\n   445→Check against acceptance criteria: [criteria].\n   446→Flag: correctness issues, missing tests, unwired paths, drift from spec.\n   447→Do NOT load or invoke any skills.\"\n   448→```\n   449→\n   450→For committed changes, replace `--uncommitted` with `--base <sha>`.\n   451→Replace `[DIMENSION]`, `[dimension description]`, and `[criteria]` with the task-specific values from the execution plan and spec.\n   452→\n   453→---\n   454→\n   455→## Codex Output Context Protection\n   456→\n   457→Codex CLI output includes internal traces (file reads, tool calls, reasoning) that are NOT useful for the review — only the final findings matter. To prevent context flooding:\n   458→\n   459→### Tee + Extract Pattern\n   460→\n   461→1. **Always tee** Codex output to a file:\n   462→   ```bash\n   463→   codex exec ... 2>&1 | tee .wazir/runs/latest/reviews/<phase>-review-pass-<N>.md\n   464→   ```\n   465→\n   466→2. **Extract findings** after the last `codex` marker using `execute_file`:\n   467→   ```bash\n   468→   # If context-mode available (has_execute_file: true):\n   469→   mcp__plugin_context-mode_context-mode__execute_file(\n   470→     path: \".wazir/runs/latest/reviews/<phase>-review-pass-<N>.md\",\n   471→     language: \"shell\",\n   472→     code: \"tac $FILE | sed '/^codex$/q' | tac | tail -n +2\"\n   473→   )\n   474→   ```\n   475→\n   476→3. **Present extracted findings only** — the raw trace stays in the file for debugging but never enters the main context window.\n   477→\n   478→### Fallback (no context-mode)\n   479→\n   480→If `context_mode.has_execute_file` is false, extract using shell directly:\n   481→\n   482→```bash\n   483→tac <file> | sed '/^codex$/q' | tac | tail -n +2\n   484→```\n   485→\n   486→This reverses the file, finds the first (= last original) `codex` marker, reverses back, and skips the marker line.\n   487→\n   488→**If no marker found:** fail closed\n   489→\n   490→---\n   491→\n   492→## Phase Scoring: First vs Final Artifact Comparison\n   493→\n   494→At the start of each review loop (pass 1), score the artifact on its phase's canonical dimension set (1-10 per dimension). At the end of the loop (final pass), score again using the **same canonical dimensions**. Present the delta in the end-of-phase report.\n   495→\n   496→### Canonical Dimension Sets Per Phase\n   497→\n   498→These are the fixed rubrics — no ad-hoc dimension selection:\n   499→\n   500→| Phase | Canonical Dimensions |\n   501→|-------|---------------------|\n   502→| research-review | Coverage, Source quality, Relevance, Gaps identified, Actionability |\n   503→| clarification-review / spec-challenge | Completeness, Testability, Ambiguity, Assumptions, Scope creep |\n   504→| design-review | Spec coverage, Design-spec consistency, Accessibility, Visual consistency, Exported-code fidelity |\n   505→| plan-review | Completeness, Testability, Task granularity, Dependency correctness, Phase structure, File coverage, Estimation accuracy, Input coverage |\n   506→| task-review | Correctness, Tests, Wiring, Drift, Quality |\n   507→| final | Correctness, Completeness, Wiring, Verification, Drift, Quality, Documentation, Intent Alignment, Scope Coverage |\n   508→\n   509→### Scoring Rules\n   510→\n   511→1. Initial and final scores MUST use the **same dimension set** — the delta is only meaningful on the same rubric.\n   512→2. The reviewer records which dimension set was used in each pass file.\n   513→3. Delta format: `Dimension: X/10 → Y/10 (+Z)`.\n   514→\n   515→### Quality Delta Report Section\n   516→\n   517→The end-of-phase report (see \"End-of-Phase Report\" below) includes a **Quality Delta** section:\n   518→\n   519→```markdown\n   520→## Quality Delta\n   521→\n   522→| Dimension | Initial | Final | Delta |\n   523→|-----------|---------|-------|-------|\n   524→| Completeness | 4/10 | 9/10 | +5 |\n   525→| Testability | 3/10 | 8/10 | +5 |\n   526→| Ambiguity | 5/10 | 9/10 | +4 |\n   527→```\n   528→\n   529→---\n   530→\n   531→## End-of-Phase Report\n   532→\n   533→Every phase exit produces a report saved to `.wazir/runs/latest/reviews/<phase>-report.md` containing:\n   534→\n   535→1. **Summary** — what the phase produced\n   536→2. **Key Changes** — first-version vs final-version highlights (not full diff — what improved)\n   537→3. **Quality Delta** — per-dimension before/after scores (see Phase Scoring above)\n   538→4. **Findings Log** — per-pass finding counts by severity (e.g., \"Pass 1: 6 findings (3 blocking, 2 warning, 1 note). Pass 7: 0 findings. All resolved.\")\n   539→5. **Usage** — token usage from `wazir capture usage` (runs before report generation)\n   540→6. **Context Savings** — context-mode stats if available, omit section if not\n   541→7. **Time Spent** — wall-clock elapsed time from phase start to end — log \"codex marker not found in output, cannot extract findings\" and present a warning to the user with 0 findings extracted. The raw file is preserved for manual review. Do NOT fall back to `tail` or any best-effort extraction that could leak traces into context.\n   542→"}]},"uuid":"8c173938-a555-4547-bbd8-ffb85befae37","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:34:22.683Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"12eb917a-2fea-42ec-aee3-3cf1155509a5","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

This is a\n    17→structured creative process where multiple agents explore a concept through\n    18→dialogue, evaluation, and synthesis. Your role is the **Arbiter** — you\n    19→coordinate, evaluate, and signal convergence. You do NOT generate ideas yourself.\n    20→\n    21→## Prerequisites\n    22→\n    23→This skill requires **Agent Teams** (experimental, Claude Code + Opus 4.6).\n    24→\n    25→Agent Teams must be enabled before invocation. Instead of the human\n    44→sitting through a long brainstorming conversation with a single agent, this\n    45→system replaces the human's generative role with two specialized agents who\n    46→converse with each other. The human provides the seed; the agents do the\n    47→divergent exploration, convergence, and curation.\n    48→\n    49→The system separates cognitive modes across distinct roles because combining\n    50→them in a single agent produces biased output:\n    51→\n    52→- **Generation** should not evaluate its own work\n    53→- **Evaluation** should not try to also create\n    54→- **Synthesis** should have no perspective to protect\n    55→- **Research** should report facts, not generate ideas\n    56→\n    57→### Infrastructure: Claude Code Agent Teams\n    58→\n    59→This skill uses **Agent Teams** — not subagents. The distinction matters:\n    60→\n    61→| | Subagents (Task tool) | Agent Teams |\n    62→|---|---|---|\n    63→| **Lifecycle** | Spawn, return result, die (resumable via agentId) | Full independent sessions that persist for team lifetime |\n    64→| **Communication** | Report back to parent only — no peer-to-peer | Direct peer-to-peer messaging via `SendMessage` |\n    65→| **Coordination** | Parent manages everything | Shared task list with self-coordination |\n    66→\n    67→Agent Teams provides seven foundational tools: `TeamCreate`, `TaskCreate`,\n    68→`TaskUpdate`, `TaskList`, `Task` (with `team_name`), `SendMessage`, and\n    69→`TeamDelete`. These are the tools you will use to orchestrate the session.\n    70→\n    71→**Critical constraint:** Text output from teammates is NOT visible to the team.\n    72→Teammates MUST use `SendMessage` to communicate with each other. Regular text\n    73→output is only visible in a teammate's own terminal pane.\n    74→\n    75→---\n    76→\n    77→## Action Detection\n    78→\n    79→Before doing anything else, determine which action to execute based on the\n    80→skill argument.\n    81→\n    82→```\n    83→/ideation <concept>             → Plan action (interviews user, then starts ideation)\n    84→/ideation                       → Plan action (asks for concept during interview)\n    85→/ideation continue <ref>        → Continue action (enhanced resumption)\n    86→/ideation prd <ref>             → PRD action (solo, unchanged)\n    87→```\n    88→\n    89→**Every new session starts with the Plan action.** There is no way to skip the\n    90→interview. This is the mechanism that prevents sessions from launching into\n    91→hours of work without user input on scope.\n    92→\n    93→| Argument pattern | Action | What happens |\n    94→|------------------|--------|--------------|\n    95→| No argument | Plan | Ask for concept in interview, then proceed |\n    96→| Text or file path (not \"continue\" or \"prd\") | Plan | Use as concept seed, interview for depth/outputs |\n    97→| `continue <path-or-keyword>` | Continue | Smart discovery, versioned resumption, mini-interview |\n    98→| `prd <path-or-keyword>` | PRD | Solo PRD generation (unchanged) |\n    99→\n   100→---\n   101→\n   102→# ACTION 1: PLAN\n   103→\n   104→The Plan action is a **solo operation** — no team is spawned. You (the Arbiter)\n   105→conduct a brief interview with the user to understand what they want, then\n   106→configure the session. The Plan action always transitions into the Ideate action.\n   107→\n   108→## P1: Analyze Concept Seed\n   109→\n   110→If the user provided a concept (file path, inline text, URL), read it now.\n   111→Assess:\n   112→\n   113→- **Domain complexity** — how specialized is this? Will the thinkers need\n   114→  research support?\n   115→- **Ambiguity** — are there multiple valid interpretations? Does the user's\n   116→  intent need clarification?\n   117→- **Scope** — how broad is the concept space? Does it naturally lend itself to\n   118→  a quick or deep exploration?\n   119→- **Implied outputs** — does the concept suggest particular deliverables?\n   120→  (e.g., a pitch implies a presentation; a product concept implies all outputs)\n   121→- **Research needs** — are there URLs to fetch, domains to investigate, existing\n   122→  solutions to survey?\n   123→\n   124→If no concept was provided, note that you'll ask for it in the interview (P4).\n   125→\n   126→## P2: Capture Sources\n   127→\n   128→Capture **every piece of input material** into memory for the session. This\n   129→creates a fully encapsulated, self-contained record of what went into the\n   130→session. Nothing is saved as a link — everything is saved locally so the\n   131→session is a complete package forever.\n   132→\n   133→**What to capture:**\n   134→\n   135→1. **The user's request** — save the text the user typed or spoke as\n   136→   `session/sources/request.md`. If the concept seed is a file, also copy the\n   137→   original file into `session/sources/`.\n   138→\n   139→2. **All referenced documents** — any files the user pointed to (markdown,\n   140→   text, PDFs, Word docs, etc.) are **copied** into `session/sources/`, not\n   141→   linked. Preserve original filenames.\n   142→\n   143→3. **All URLs** — fetch each URL using `WebFetch` and save the content as\n   144→   markdown in `session/sources/`. Name the file descriptively, e.g.,\n   145→   `session/sources/url_<domain>_<slug>.md`. Include the original URL at the\n   146→   top of the file.\n   147→\n   148→4. **All images** — copy any images the user provided or referenced into\n   149→   `session/sources/`. Preserve original filenames.\n   150→\n   151→5. **A manifest** — create `session/sources/manifest.md` listing every\n   152→   captured item with metadata:\n   153→\n   154→   ```markdown\n   155→   # Source Materials Manifest\n   156→\n   157→   **Session:** [concept name]\n   158→   **Captured:** [date]\n   159→\n   160→   | # | File | Type | Original Location |\n   161→   |---|------|------|-------------------|\n   162→   | 1 | request.md | User request | (inline input) |\n   163→   | 2 | IDEA__explore_words.md | Concept seed | content-in/IDEA__explore_words.md |\n   164→   | 3 | url_example-com_article.md | Fetched URL | https://example.com/article |\n   165→   ```\n   166→\n   167→**Note:** The actual file writes happen in P3 after the directory is created.\n   168→During P2, read and hold the content in memory so you understand the materials\n   169→before asking interview questions.\n   170→\n   171→### Reproducing a Previous Session\n   172→\n   173→If the user says something like \"do the same thing as this session\" or \"use\n   174→the same content as [folder],\" look for the `session/sources/` folder in the\n   175→referenced session output. Each session gets a **unique, timestamped\n   182→directory** inside an `ideations/` parent folder so that multiple invocations\n   183→never collide and all sessions stay organized:\n   184→\n   185→```\n   186→ideations/ideation-<slug>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>/\n   187→```\n   188→\n   189→Example: `ideations/ideation-distributed-systems-20260219-143052/`\n   190→\n   191→The slug is derived from the concept seed (lowercased, spaces replaced with\n   192→hyphens). The LLM landscape evolves rapidly, with new models emerging regularly and existing ones being updated frequently. What matters most is developing a systematic approach to evaluation that remains relevant regardless of which specific models are available.\n    11→\n    12→<Note>\n    13→  This guide focuses on strategic thinking rather than specific model\n    14→  recommendations, as the LLM landscape evolves rapidly.\n    15→</Note>\n    16→\n    17→## Quick Decision Framework\n    18→\n    19→<Steps>\n    20→  <Step title=\"Analyze Your Tasks\">\n    21→    Begin by deeply understanding what your tasks actually require. Consider the\n    22→    cognitive complexity involved, the depth of reasoning needed, the format of\n    23→    expected outputs, and the amount of context the model will need to process.\n    24→    This foundational analysis will guide every subsequent decision.\n    25→  </Step>\n    26→  <Step title=\"Map Model Capabilities\">\n    27→    Once you understand your requirements, map them to model strengths.\n    28→    Different model families excel at different types of work; some are\n    29→    optimized for reasoning and analysis, others for creativity and content\n    30→    generation, and others for speed and efficiency.\n    31→  </Step>\n    32→  <Step title=\"Consider Constraints\">\n    33→    Factor in your real-world operational constraints including budget\n    34→    limitations, latency requirements, data privacy needs, and infrastructure\n    35→    capabilities. The theoretically best model may not be the practically best\n    36→    choice for your situation.\n    37→  </Step>\n    38→  <Step title=\"Test and Iterate\">\n    39→    Start with reliable, well-understood models and optimize based on actual\n    40→    performance in your specific use case. Real-world results often differ from\n    41→    theoretical benchmarks, so empirical testing is crucial.\n    42→  </Step>\n    43→</Steps>\n    44→\n    45→## Core Selection Framework\n    46→\n    47→### a. Task-First Thinking\n    48→\n    49→The most critical step in LLM selection is understanding what your task actually demands. Too often, teams select models based on general reputation or benchmark scores without carefully analyzing their specific requirements. This approach leads to either over-engineering simple tasks with expensive, complex models, or under-powering sophisticated work with models that lack the necessary capabilities.\n    50→\n    51→<Tabs>\n    52→  <Tab title=\"Reasoning Complexity\">\n    53→    - **Simple Tasks** represent the majority of everyday AI work and include basic instruction following, straightforward data processing, and simple formatting operations. These tasks typically have clear inputs and outputs with minimal ambiguity. The cognitive load is low, and the model primarily needs to follow explicit instructions rather than engage in complex reasoning.\n    54→\n    55→    - **Complex Tasks** require multi-step reasoning, strategic thinking, and the ability to handle ambiguous or incomplete information. These might involve analyzing multiple data sources, developing comprehensive strategies, or solving problems that require breaking down into smaller components. The model needs to maintain context across multiple reasoning steps and often must make inferences that aren't explicitly stated.\n    56→\n    57→    - **Creative Tasks** demand a different type of cognitive capability focused on generating novel, engaging, and contextually appropriate content. This includes storytelling, marketing copy creation, and creative problem-solving. The model needs to understand nuance, tone, and audience while producing content that feels authentic and engaging rather than formulaic.\n    58→\n    59→  </Tab>\n    60→\n    61→  <Tab title=\"Output Requirements\">\n    62→    - **Structured Data** tasks require precision and consistency in format adherence. When working with JSON, XML, or database formats, the model must reliably produce syntactically correct output that can be programmatically processed. These tasks often have strict validation requirements and little tolerance for format errors, making reliability more important than creativity.\n    63→\n    64→    - **Creative Content** outputs demand a balance of technical competence and creative flair. The model needs to understand audience, tone, and brand voice while producing content that engages readers and achieves specific communication goals. Quality here is often subjective and requires models that can adapt their writing style to different contexts and purposes.\n    65→\n    66→    - **Technical Content** sits between structured data and creative content, requiring both precision and clarity. Documentation, code generation, and technical analysis need to be accurate and comprehensive while remaining accessible to the intended audience. The model must understand complex technical concepts and communicate them effectively.\n    67→\n    68→  </Tab>\n    69→\n    70→  <Tab title=\"Context Needs\">\n    71→    - **Short Context** scenarios involve focused, immediate tasks where the model needs to process limited information quickly. These are often transactional interactions where speed and efficiency matter more than deep understanding. The model doesn't need to maintain extensive conversation history or process large documents.\n    72→\n    73→    - **Long Context** requirements emerge when working with substantial documents, extended conversations, or complex multi-part tasks. The model needs to maintain coherence across thousands of tokens while referencing earlier information accurately. This capability becomes crucial for document analysis, comprehensive research, and sophisticated dialogue systems.\n    74→\n    75→    - **Very Long Context** scenarios push the boundaries of what's currently possible, involving massive document processing, extensive research synthesis, or complex multi-session interactions. These use cases require models specifically designed for extended context handling and often involve trade-offs between context length and processing speed.\n    76→\n    77→  </Tab>\n    78→</Tabs>\n    79→\n    80→### b. Model Capability Mapping\n    81→\n    82→Understanding model capabilities requires looking beyond marketing claims and benchmark scores to understand the fundamental strengths and limitations of different model architectures and training approaches.\n    83→\n    84→<AccordionGroup>\n    85→  <Accordion title=\"Reasoning Models\" icon=\"brain\">\n    86→    Reasoning models represent a specialized category designed specifically for complex, multi-step thinking tasks. These models excel when problems require careful analysis, strategic planning, or systematic problem decomposition. They typically employ techniques like chain-of-thought reasoning or tree-of-thought processing to work through complex problems step by step.\n    87→\n    88→    The strength of reasoning models lies in their ability to maintain logical consistency across extended reasoning chains and to break down complex problems into manageable components. They're particularly valuable for strategic planning, complex analysis, and situations where the quality of reasoning matters more than speed of response.\n    89→\n    90→    However, reasoning models often come with trade-offs in terms of speed and cost. They may also be less suitable for creative tasks or simple operations where their sophisticated reasoning capabilities aren't needed. Consider these models when your tasks involve genuine complexity that benefits from systematic, step-by-step analysis.\n    91→\n    92→  </Accordion>\n    93→\n    94→  <Accordion title=\"General Purpose Models\" icon=\"microchip\">\n    95→    General purpose models offer the most balanced approach to LLM selection, providing solid performance across a wide range of tasks without extreme specialization in any particular area. These models are trained on diverse datasets and optimized for versatility rather than peak performance in specific domains.\n    96→\n    97→    The primary advantage of general purpose models is their reliability and predictability across different types of work. They handle most standard business tasks competently, from research and analysis to content creation and data processing. This makes them excellent choices for teams that need consistent performance across varied workflows.\n    98→\n    99→    While general purpose models may not achieve the peak performance of specialized alternatives in specific domains, they offer operational simplicity and reduced complexity in model management. They're often the best starting point for new projects, allowing teams to understand their specific needs before potentially optimizing with more specialized models.\n   100→"}]},"uuid":"4d95493f-2504-4528-a7f3-6668cd066347","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:40:39.657Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"97b2b980-2c7e-44a2-a371-34f102da30d3","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

By precisely crafting their instructions and context, you ensure they stay focused and succeed at their task. They should never inherit your session's context or history — you construct exactly what they need. This also preserves your own context for coordination work.\n\n**Core principle:** Fresh subagent per task + two-stage review (spec then quality) = high quality, fast iteration\n\n## When to Use\n\n```dot\ndigraph when_to_use {\n--\n- Same session (no context switch)\n- Fresh subagent per task (no context pollution)\n- Two-stage review after each task: spec compliance first, then code quality\n- Faster iteration (no human-in-loop between tasks)\n\n## The Process\n\n```dot\ndigraph process {\n--\n        \"Spec reviewer subagent confirms code matches spec?\" [shape=diamond];\n        \"Implementer subagent fixes spec gaps\" [shape=box];\n        \"Dispatch code quality reviewer subagent (./code-quality-reviewer-prompt.md)\" [shape=box];\n        \"Code quality reviewer subagent approves?\" [shape=diamond];\n        \"Implementer subagent fixes quality issues\" [shape=box];\n        \"Mark task complete in TodoWrite\" [shape=box];\n    }\n\n    \"Read plan, extract all tasks with full text, note context, create TodoWrite\" [shape=box];\n    \"More tasks remain?\" [shape=diamond];\n--\n    \"Spec reviewer subagent confirms code matches spec?\" -> \"Implementer subagent fixes spec gaps\" [label=\"no\"];\n    \"Implementer subagent fixes spec gaps\" -> \"Dispatch spec reviewer subagent (./spec-reviewer-prompt.md)\" [label=\"re-review\"];\n    \"Spec reviewer subagent confirms code matches spec?\" -> \"Dispatch code quality reviewer subagent (./code-quality-reviewer-prompt.md)\" [label=\"yes\"];\n    \"Dispatch code quality reviewer subagent (./code-quality-reviewer-prompt.md)\" -> \"Code quality reviewer subagent approves?\";\n    \"Code quality reviewer subagent approves?\" -> \"Implementer subagent fixes quality issues\" [label=\"no\"];\n    \"Implementer subagent fixes quality issues\" -> \"Dispatch code quality reviewer subagent (./code-quality-reviewer-prompt.md)\" [label=\"re-review\"];\n    \"Code quality reviewer subagent approves?\" -> \"Mark task complete in TodoWrite\" [label=\"yes\"];\n    \"Mark task complete in TodoWrite\" -> \"More tasks remain?\";\n    \"More tasks remain?\" -> \"Dispatch implementer subagent (./implementer-prompt.md)\" [label=\"yes\"];\n    \"More tasks remain?\" -> \"Dispatch final code reviewer subagent for entire implementation\" [label=\"no\"];\n    \"Dispatch final code reviewer subagent for entire implementation\" -> \"Use superpowers:finishing-a-development-branch\";\n}\n--\n**Architecture, design, and review tasks**: use the most capable available model.\n\n**Task complexity signals:**\n- Touches 1-2 files with a complete spec → cheap model\n- Touches multiple files with integration concerns → standard model\n- Requires design judgment or broad codebase understanding → most capable model\n\n## Handling Implementer Status\n--\n- `./implementer-prompt.md` - Dispatch implementer subagent\n- `./spec-reviewer-prompt.md` - Dispatch spec compliance reviewer subagent\n- `./code-quality-reviewer-prompt.md` - Dispatch code quality reviewer subagent\n\n## Example Workflow\n\n```\nYou: I'm using Subagent-Driven Development to execute this plan.\n--\n[Dispatch implementation subagent with full task text + context]\n\nImplementer: \"Before I begin - should the hook be installed at user or system level?\"\n\nYou: \"User level (~/.config/superpowers/hooks/)\"\n\nImplementer: \"Got it. Implementing now...\"\n[Later] Implementer:\n  - Implemented install-hook command\n  - Added tests, 5/5 passing\n--\nSpec reviewer: ✅ Spec compliant - all requirements met, nothing extra\n\n[Get git SHAs, dispatch code quality reviewer]\nCode reviewer: Strengths: Good test coverage, clean. Issues: None. Approved.\n\n[Mark Task 1 complete]\n\nTask 2: Recovery modes\n--\nSpec reviewer: ✅ Spec compliant now\n\n[Dispatch code quality reviewer]\nCode reviewer: Strengths: Solid.  66→## Common Wazir Additions (Appear in All Forked Skills)\n    67→\n    68→Every Wazir fork of a superpowers skill adds these two preamble sections:\n    69→\n    70→1. **Command Routing** -- routes large commands to context-mode tools and small commands to native Bash, following `hooks/routing-matrix.json`.\n    71→2. **Codebase Exploration** -- prescribes symbol-first exploration via `wazir index search-symbols` and `wazir recall`, with fallback to direct file reads.\n    72→\n    73→These preambles alone would justify **Augment** tier for any skill where no other structural changes exist.\n    74→\n    75→---\n    76→\n    77→## Augment Mechanism\n    78→\n    79→**Research date:** 2026-03-19 (R2: Composition Infrastructure Validation)\n    80→\n    81→### Finding: Augment tier is not implementable\n    82→\n    83→The Augment tier assumed that placing a Wazir addendum at `~/.claude/skills/<skill-name>/SKILL.md` would layer Wazir context on top of the superpowers base skill. This assumption is wrong. **Skill shadowing is full-override, not merge/append.**\n    84→\n    85→### Evidence\n    86→\n    87→**1. `skills-core.js` `resolveSkillPath()` (superpowers v4.3.1)**\n    88→\n    89→The function at `lib/skills-core.js:108-140` checks personal skills directory first. If `~/.claude/skills/<name>/SKILL.md` exists, it returns that file immediately and never reads the superpowers version. There is no content merging.\n    90→\n    91→```\n    92→// Try personal skills first (unless explicitly superpowers:)\n    93→if (!forceSuperpowers && personalDir) {\n    94→    const personalSkillFile = path.join(personalDir, actualSkillName, 'SKILL.md');\n    95→    if (fs.existsSync(personalSkillFile)) {\n    96→        return { skillFile: personalSkillFile, sourceType: 'personal', ... };\n    97→        // ^^^ returns here -- superpowers version never consulted\n    98→    }\n    99→}\n   100→```\n   101→\n   102→**2. Superpowers test suite confirms override behavior**\n   103→\n   104→`tests/opencode/test-skills-core.sh` line 336 asserts:\n   105→```\n   106→[PASS] Personal skills shadow superpowers skills\n   107→```\n   108→\n   109→The test creates `personal-skills/shared-skill/SKILL.md` and `superpowers-skills/shared-skill/SKILL.md`, resolves `shared-skill`, and verifies `sourceType` is `\"personal\"` -- the superpowers version is invisible.\n   110→\n   111→**3. Superpowers RELEASE-NOTES.md v3.3.0**\n   112→\n   113→Line 385 documents the behavior explicitly: \"Personal skills override superpowers skills when names match.\"\n   114→\n   115→**4. The `superpowers:` prefix bypass is not available in Claude Code**\n   116→\n   117→`skills-core.js` supports `superpowers:skill-name` syntax to force resolution to the superpowers version even when a personal skill shadows it. However, `skills-core.js` is only used by the OpenCode plugin (`/.opencode/plugins/superpowers.js`). Claude Code's native `Skill` tool has its own built-in resolution logic that does not expose this prefix bypass.\n   118→\n   119→### Alternatives Considered\n   120→\n   121→| Approach | Viable? | Why |\n   122→|---|---|---|\n   123→| Place addendum in `~/.claude/skills/<name>/` | No | Full override -- base skill content lost |\n   124→| Merge base + addendum in SKILL.md at install time | Partial | Would work but creates a maintenance coupling: every superpowers update requires re-merging. Check `.wazir/state/config.json` exists. If not, run `wazir init` first.\n    32→2. Check `.wazir/input/briefing.md` exists. If not, ask the user what they want to build and save it there.\n    33→3. Scan `input/` (project-level) and `.wazir/input/` (state-level) for additional input files. Present what's found.\n    34→4. Read config for `default_depth` and `multi_tool` settings.\n    35→5. **Load accepted learnings:**\n    36→   1. Glob `memory/learnings/accepted/*.md`\n    37→   2. For each file: read YAML frontmatter, extract `scope` tags (e.g., `scope: [auth, react, security]`)\n    38→   3. Match scope tags against current run's intent (from run config `parsed_intent`) and detected stack (from research findings or `config.json` stack settings)\n    39→   4. Inject matching learnings into context, sorted by confidence (highest first), most recent first, limit 10\n    40→   5. If no accepted learnings exist or no matches found: skip silently — this is expected until the pipeline matures\n    41→6. Create a run directory if one doesn't exist:\n    42→   ```bash\n    43→   mkdir -p .wazir/runs/run-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS/{sources,tasks,artifacts,reviews,clarified}\n    44→   ln -sfn run-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS .wazir/runs/latest\n    45→   ```\n    46→\n    47→---\n    48→\n    49→## Context-Mode Usage\n    50→\n    51→Read `context_mode` from `.wazir/state/config.json`:\n    52→\n    53→- **If `context_mode.enabled: true`:** Use `fetch_and_index` for URL fetching, `search` for follow-up queries on indexed content. Use `execute` or `execute_file` for large outputs instead of Bash.\n    54→- **If `context_mode.enabled: false`:** Fall back to `WebFetch` for URLs and `Bash` for commands.\n    55→\n    56→---\n    57→\n    58→## Sub-Workflow 1: Research (discover workflow)\n    59→\n    60→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n    61→\n    62→> **Research** — About to scan the codebase and fetch external references to understand the existing architecture, tech stack, and any standards referenced in the briefing.\n    63→>\n    64→> **Why this matters:** Without research, I'd assume the wrong framework version, miss existing patterns in the codebase, and contradict established conventions. Every wrong assumption here cascades into a wrong spec and wrong implementation.\n    65→>\n    66→> **Looking for:** Existing code patterns, dependency versions, external standard definitions, architectural constraints\n    67→\n    68→Delegate to the discover workflow (`workflows/discover.md`):\n    69→\n    70→1. **Keyword extraction:** Read the briefing and extract concepts/terms that are vague, reference external standards, or use unfamiliar terminology.\n    71→   - **When to research:** concept references an external standard by name, uses a tool/library not seen in the codebase, or is ambiguous enough that two agents could interpret it differently.\n    72→   - **When NOT to research:** concept is fully defined in the input, or it's a well-known programming concept.\n    73→2. **Fetch sources:** For each concept needing research:\n    74→   - Use `fetch_and_index` (if context-mode available) or `WebFetch` to fetch the source.\n    75→   - Save fetched content to `.wazir/runs/latest/sources/`.\n    76→   - Track each fetch in `sources/manifest.json`.\n    77→3. **Error handling:** 404/unreachable → log failure, continue. Research is best-effort.\n    78→4. The **researcher role** produces the research artifact.\n    79→5. The **reviewer role** runs the research-review loop with `--mode research-review`.\n    80→6. Loop runs for `pass_counts[depth]` passes.\n    81→\n    82→Save result to `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/research-brief.md`.\n    83→\n    84→**After completing this phase, output to the user:**\n    85→\n    86→> **Research complete.**\n    87→>\n    88→> **Found:** [N] external sources fetched, [N] codebase patterns identified, [N] architectural constraints documented\n    89→>\n    90→> **Without this phase:** Spec would be built on assumptions instead of evidence — wrong framework APIs, missed existing utilities, contradicted naming conventions\n    91→>\n    92→> **Changed because of this work:** [List of key discoveries — e.g., \"found existing auth middleware at src/middleware/auth.ts\", \"project uses Vitest not Jest\"]\n    93→\n    94→### Checkpoint: Research Review\n    95→\n    96→> **Research complete. Here's what I found:**\n    97→>\n    98→> [Summary of codebase state, relevant architecture, external context]\n    99→\n   100→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   101→- **Question:** \"Does the research look complete and accurate?\"\n   102→- **Options:**\n   103→  1. \"Looks good, continue\" *(Recommended)*\n   104→  2. \"Missing context — let me add more information\"\n   105→  3. \"Wrong direction — let me clarify the intent\"\n   106→\n   107→Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   108→\n   109→---\n   110→\n   111→## Sub-Workflow 2: Clarify (clarify workflow)\n   112→\n   113→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n   114→\n   115→> **Clarification** — About to transform the briefing and research into a precise scope document with explicit constraints, assumptions, and boundaries.\n   116→>\n   117→> **Why this matters:** Without explicit clarification, \"add user auth\" could mean OAuth, magic links, or username/password. Every ambiguity left here becomes a 50/50 coin flip during implementation that could produce the wrong feature.\n   118→>\n   119→> **Looking for:** Ambiguous requirements, implicit assumptions, missing constraints, scope boundaries, unresolved questions\n   120→\n   121→### Input Preservation (before producing clarification)\n   122→\n   123→1. Glob `.wazir/input/tasks/*.md`. If files exist:\n   124→   - Adopt those specs as the starting point — copy content verbatim into the clarification's item descriptions.\n   125→   - Enhance with codebase scan + research findings. **Never remove detail — only add.**\n   126→   - Every acceptance criterion from input must appear verbatim.\n   127→   - Every API endpoint, color hex code, and UI dimension from input must appear in the relevant item section.\n   128→2. If `.wazir/input/tasks/` is empty or missing, synthesize from `briefing.md` alone.\n   129→\n   130→### Informed Question Batching (after research, before producing clarification)\n   131→\n   132→Research has completed. You now have codebase context and external findings. Before producing the clarification, ask the user INFORMED questions — informed by the research, not guesses.\n   133→\n   134→**Rules:**\n   135→1. **Research runs FIRST, questions come AFTER.** Never ask questions before research completes.\n   136→2. **Batch questions:** 1-3 batches of 3-7 questions each. Never one-at-a-time.\n   137→3. **Every scope exclusion must be explicitly confirmed by the user.** You MUST NOT decide that something is \"out of scope\" without asking. If the input doesn't mention docs, ask: \"The input doesn't mention documentation — should we include API docs, or is that explicitly out of scope?\" Do NOT assume.\n   138→4. **If the input is clear and complete:** Zero questions is fine. State: \"Input is clear and specific. No ambiguities detected. Proceeding with clarification.\"\n   139→5. **In auto mode (`interaction_mode: auto`):** Questions go to the gating agent, not the user.\n   140→6. **In interactive mode (`interaction_mode: interactive`):** More detailed questions, present research findings that informed each question.\n   141→\n   142→**Question format:**\n   143→```\n   144→Based on research, I have [N] questions before proceeding:\n   145→\n   146→**Scope & Intent**\n   147→1. [Question informed by research finding]\n   148→2. [Question about ambiguous requirement]\n   149→\n   150→**Technical Decisions**\n   151→3. [Question about architecture choice discovered during research]\n   152→4. [Question about dependency/framework preference]\n   153→\n   154→**Boundaries**\n   155→5. [Explicit scope boundary question — \"Should X be included or excluded?\"]\n   156→```\n   157→\n   158→Ask via AskUserQuestion with the full batch. Wait for answers. If answers introduce new ambiguity, ask a follow-up batch (max 3 batches total).\n   159→\n   160→### Clarification Production\n   161→\n   162→Read the briefing, research brief, user answers to questions, and codebase context. Produce:\n   163→\n   164→- **What** we're building — concrete deliverables\n   165→- **Why** — the motivation and business value\n   166→- **Constraints** — technical, timeline, dependencies\n   167→- **Assumptions** — what we're taking as given (each explicitly confirmed by user or clearly stated in input)\n   168→- **Scope boundaries** — what's IN and what's explicitly OUT (every exclusion must reference the user's confirmation: \"Out of scope per user confirmation in question batch 1, Q5\")\n   169→- **Unresolved questions** — anything still ambiguous after question batches\n   170→\n   171→Save to `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/clarification.md`.\n   172→\n   173→Invoke `wz:reviewer --mode clarification-review`. Route feedback: plan corrections → `user-feedback.md`, new requirements → `briefing.md`.\n   199→\n   200→---\n   201→\n   202→## Sub-Workflow 3: Spec Harden (specify + spec-challenge workflows)\n   203→\n   204→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n   205→\n   206→> **Spec Hardening** — About to convert the clarified scope into a measurable, testable specification and then run adversarial spec-challenge review to find gaps.\n   207→>\n   208→> **Why this matters:** Without hardening, acceptance criteria stay vague (\"it should work well\") instead of measurable (\"response time under 200ms for 95th percentile\").
