The executor's per-task reviewer already validated against task specs — that concern is covered. The final reviewer catches drift: does what we built match what the user actually asked for?\n    33→\n    34→**Reviewer-owned responsibilities** (callers must NOT replicate these):\n    35→1. **Two-tier review** — internal review first (fast, cheap, expertise-loaded), Codex second (fresh eyes on clean code)\n    36→2. **Dimension selection** — the reviewer selects the correct dimension set for the review mode and depth\n    37→3. **Pass counting** — the reviewer tracks pass numbers and enforces the depth-based cap (quick=3, standard=5, deep=7)\n    38→4. **Finding attribution** — each finding is tagged `[Internal]`, `[Codex]`, or `[Both]` based on source\n    39→5. **Dimension set recording** — each review pass file records which canonical dimension set was used, enabling Phase Scoring (first vs final delta)\n    40→6. **Learning pipeline** — ALL findings (internal + Codex) feed into `state.sqlite` and the learning system\n    41→\n    42→## Review Modes\n    43→\n    44→The reviewer operates in different modes depending on the phase. Mode MUST be passed explicitly by the caller (`--mode <mode>`). The reviewer does NOT auto-detect mode from artifact availability. If `--mode` is not provided, ask the user which review to run.\n    45→\n    46→| Mode | Invoked during | Prerequisites | Dimensions | Output |\n    47→|------|---------------|---------------|------------|--------|\n    48→| `final` | After execution + verification | Completed task artifacts, approved spec/plan/design | 9 final-review dims, scored 0-90 | Scored verdict (PASS/FAIL) |\n    49→| `spec-challenge` | After specify | Draft spec artifact | 5 spec/clarification dims | Pass/fix loop, no score |\n    50→| `design-review` | After design approval | Design artifact, approved spec | 5 design-review dims (canonical) | Pass/fix loop, no score |\n    51→| `plan-review` | After planning | Draft plan artifact | 8 plan dims (7 + input coverage) | Pass/fix loop, no score |\n    52→| `task-review` | During execution, per task | Uncommitted changes or `--base` SHA | 5 task-execution dims (correctness, tests, wiring, drift, quality) | Pass/fix loop, no score |\n    53→| `research-review` | During discover | Research artifact | 5 research dims | Pass/fix loop, no score |\n    54→| `clarification-review` | During clarify | Clarification artifact | 5 spec/clarification dims | Pass/fix loop, no score |\n    55→\n    56→Each mode follows the review loop pattern in `docs/reference/review-loop-pattern.md`. Pass counts are fixed by depth (quick=3, standard=5, deep=7). No extension.\n    57→\n    58→### CHANGELOG Enforcement\n    59→\n    60→In `task-review` and `final` modes, flag missing CHANGELOG entries for user-facing changes as **[warning]** severity. User-facing changes include new features, behavior changes, and bug fixes visible to users. Internal changes (refactors, tooling, tests) do not require CHANGELOG entries.\n    61→\n    62→## Prerequisites\n    63→\n    64→Prerequisites depend on the review mode:\n    65→\n    66→### `final` mode\n    67→\n    68→**Phase Prerequisites (Hard Gate):** Before proceeding, verify ALL of these artifacts exist. If ANY is missing, **STOP** and report which are missing.\n    69→\n    70→- [ ] `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/clarification.md`\n    71→- [ ] `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/spec-hardened.md`\n    72→- [ ] `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/design.md`\n    73→- [ ] `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/execution-plan.md`\n    74→- [ ] `.wazir/runs/latest/artifacts/verification-proof.md`\n    75→\n    76→If any file is missing:\n    77→\n    78→> **Cannot run final review: missing prerequisite artifacts.**\n    79→>\n    80→> Missing: [list missing files]\n    81→>\n    82→> Run `/wazir:clarifier` (for clarified/* files) or `/wazir:executor` (for verification-proof.md) first.\n    83→\n    84→1. Check `.wazir/runs/latest/artifacts/` has completed task artifacts. If not, tell the user to run `/wazir:executor` first.\n    85→2. Read the approved spec, plan, and design from `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/`.\n    86→3. Read `.wazir/state/config.json` for depth and multi_tool settings.\n    87→\n    88→### `task-review` mode\n    89→1. Uncommitted changes exist for the current task, or a `--base` SHA is provided for committed changes.\n    90→2. Read `.wazir/state/config.json` for depth and multi_tool settings.\n    91→3. **Commit discipline check:** If uncommitted changes span work from multiple tasks (e.g., files from task N and task N+1 are both modified), REJECT immediately: \"REJECTED: Multiple tasks in single commit. Split into per-task commits before review.\" This is a blocking finding — no other dimensions are evaluated until resolved.\n    92→4. **Security sensitivity check:** Run `detectSecurityPatterns` from `tooling/src/checks/security-sensitivity.js` against the diff. If `triggered === true`, add the 6 security review dimensions (injection, auth bypass, data exposure, CSRF/SSRF, XSS, secrets leakage) to the standard 5 task-execution dimensions for this review pass. Security findings use severity levels: critical (exploitable), high (likely exploitable), medium (defense-in-depth gap), low (best-practice deviation).\n    93→\n    94→### `spec-challenge`, `design-review`, `plan-review`, `research-review`, `clarification-review` modes\n    95→1. The appropriate input artifact for the mode exists.\n    96→2. Read `.wazir/state/config.json` for depth and multi_tool settings.\n    97→3. **`plan-review` additional dimension — Input Coverage:**\n    98→   - Read the original input/briefing from `.wazir/input/briefing.md` and any `input/*.md` files\n    99→   - Count distinct items/requirements in the input\n   100→   - Count tasks in the execution plan\n   101→   - If `tasks_in_plan < items_in_input` → **HIGH** finding: \"Plan covers [N] of [M] input items. Missing: [list of uncovered items]\"\n   102→   - If `tasks_in_plan >= items_in_input` → dimension passes\n   103→   - One task MAY cover multiple input items if justified in the task description\n   104→   - This is the review-level enforcement of the \"no scope reduction\" rule\n   105→\n   106→## Review Process (`final` mode)\n   107→\n   108→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n   109→\n   110→> **Final Review** — About to run adversarial 9-dimension review comparing your implementation against the original input, not just the task specs. The executor's per-task reviewer already validated correctness per-task — this catches drift between what you asked for and what was actually built.\n   111→>\n   112→> **Why this matters:** Without this, implementation drift ships undetected. Per-task review confirms each task matches its spec, but cannot catch: tasks that collectively miss the original intent, scope creep that added unrequested features, or acceptance criteria that were rewritten to match implementation instead of input.\n   113→>\n   114→> **Looking for:** Logic errors, missing features, dead code, unsubstantiated \"it works\" claims, scope creep, security gaps, stale documentation\n   115→\n   116→**Input:** Read the ORIGINAL user input (`.wazir/input/briefing.md`, `input/` directory files) and compare against what was built. This catches intent drift that task-level review misses.\n   117→\n   118→### Input Sources (read before scoring)\n   119→1. Read the original input: `.wazir/input/briefing.md` or `.wazir/runs/<id>/sources/input.md`\n   120→2. Read user feedback: `.wazir/runs/<id>/user-input-log.ndjson` (parse each JSON line)\n   121→3. Count distinct items/requirements in the original input\n   122→4. If `user-input-log.ndjson` does not exist: log a finding — \"User input not captured — cannot verify intent alignment\" (severity: warning)\n   123→\n   124→Perform adversarial review across 9 dimensions:\n   125→\n   126→1. **Correctness** — Does the code do what the original input asked for? *(catches: logic errors, wrong behavior, spec violations)*\n   127→2. **Completeness** — Are all requirements from the original input met? *(catches: missing features, unimplemented acceptance criteria, partially delivered items)*\n   128→3. **Wiring** — Are all paths connected end-to-end? *(catches: dead code, disconnected paths, missing imports, orphaned routes)*\n   129→4. **Verification** — Is there evidence (tests, type checks) for each claim? *(catches: false claims of \"it works\" without evidence, untested code paths, missing type coverage)*\n   130→5. **Drift** — Does the implementation match what the user originally requested? (not just the plan — the INPUT) *(catches: scope creep, plan deviations, unauthorized changes, gold-plating)*\n   131→6. **Quality** — Code style, naming, error handling, security *(catches: security vulnerabilities, poor error handling, inconsistent naming, missing input validation)*\n   132→7. **Documentation** — Changelog entries, commit messages, comments *(catches: missing changelogs, wrong commit messages, stale comments, undocumented breaking changes)*\n   133→8. **Intent Alignment** — Does the implementation match what the user originally asked for, including any mid-run corrections from `user-input-log.ndjson`? Compare against the RAW INPUT, not the spec (which may have drifted). Score 0 if implementation contradicts a user correction. *(catches: spec drift from user intent, ignored user corrections, misinterpreted requirements)*\n   134→9. **Scope Coverage** — Count distinct items in the original input. Count items implemented (via commits/diffs). If any input item is missing from the implementation, flag as HIGH finding with the specific missing item. Score = (implemented items / input items) * 10. *(catches: dropped requirements, partial delivery, silent scope reduction)*\n   135→\n   136→## Context Retrieval\n   137→\n   138→- Read the diff first (primary input)\n   139→- Use `wazir index search-symbols <name>` to locate related code\n   140→- Use `wazir recall symbol <name-or-id> --tier L1` to check structural alignment\n   141→- Read files directly for: logic errors, missing edge cases, integration concerns\n   142→\n   143→## Scoring (`final` mode)\n   144→\n   145→Score each dimension 0-10. Total out of 90 (9 dimensions x 10 each).\n   146→\n   147→| Verdict | Score | Action |\n   148→|---------|-------|--------|\n   149→| **PASS** | 72+ | Ready for PR or merge |\n   150→| **NEEDS MINOR FIXES** | 54-71 | Auto-fix and re-review |\n   151→| **NEEDS REWORK** | 36-53 | Re-run affected tasks |\n   152→| **FAIL** | 0-35 | Fundamental issues |\n   153→\n   154→## Two-Tier Review Flow\n   155→\n   156→The review process has two tiers. Internal review catches ~80% of issues quickly and cheaply. Codex review provides fresh eyes on clean code.\n   157→\n   158→### Tier 1: Internal Review (Fast, Cheap, Expertise-Loaded)\n   159→\n   160→1. **Compose expertise:** Load relevant expertise modules from `expertise/composition-map.yaml` into context based on the review mode and detected stack. This gives the internal reviewer domain-specific knowledge.\n   161→2. **Run internal review** using the dimension set for the current mode. When multi-model is enabled, use **Sonnet** (not Opus) for internal review passes — it's fast and good enough for pattern matching against expertise.\n   162→3. **Produce findings:** Each finding is tagged `[Internal]` with severity (blocking, warning, note).\n   163→4. **Fix cycle:** If blocking findings exist, the executor fixes them. Re-run internal review. Repeat until clean or cap reached.\n   164→\n   165→Internal review passes are logged to `.wazir/runs/latest/reviews/<mode>-internal-pass-<N>.md`.\n   166→\n   167→### Tier 2: External Review (Fresh Eyes on Clean Code)\n   168→\n   169→Only runs AFTER Tier 1 produces a clean pass (no blocking findings).\n   170→\n   171→Read `.wazir/state/config.json`. If `multi_tool.tools` includes external reviewers:\n   172→\n   173→#### Codex Review\n   174→\n   175→**For detailed Codex CLI usage, see `wz:codex-cli` skill.**\n   176→\n   177→If `codex` is in `multi_tool.tools`:\n   178→\n   179→1. Run Codex review against the current changes:\n   180→   ```bash\n   181→   CODEX_MODEL=$(jq -r '.multi_tool.codex.model // empty' .wazir/state/config.json 2>/dev/null)\n   182→   CODEX_MODEL=${CODEX_MODEL:-gpt-5.4}\n   183→   codex review -c model=\"$CODEX_MODEL\" --uncommitted --title \"Wazir review: <brief summary>\" \\\n   184→     \"Review against these acceptance criteria: <paste criteria from spec>\" \\\n   185→     2>&1 | tee .wazir/runs/latest/reviews/codex-review.md\n   186→   ```\n   187→   Or if changes are committed:\n   188→   ```bash\n   189→   CODEX_MODEL=$(jq -r '.multi_tool.codex.model // empty' .wazir/state/config.json 2>/dev/null)\n   190→   CODEX_MODEL=${CODEX_MODEL:-gpt-5.4}\n   191→   codex review -c model=\"$CODEX_MODEL\" --base <base-branch> --title \"Wazir review: <brief summary>\" \\\n   192→     \"Review against these acceptance criteria: <paste criteria from spec>\" \\\n   193→     2>&1 | tee .wazir/runs/latest/reviews/codex-review.md\n   194→   ```\n   195→\n   196→2. **Extract findings only** (context protection): After tee, use `execute_file` to extract only the final findings from the Codex output (everything after the last `codex` marker). If context-mode is unavailable, use `tac <file> | sed '/^codex$/q' | tac | tail -n +2`. If no marker found, fail closed (0 findings, warn user). See `docs/reference/review-loop-pattern.md` \"Codex Output Context Protection\" for full protocol.\n   197→3. Incorporate extracted Codex findings into your scoring — if Codex flags something you missed, add it. If you disagree with a Codex finding, note it with your rationale.\n   198→\n   199→**Codex error handling:** If codex exits non-zero (auth/rate-limit/transport failure), log the full stderr, mark the pass as `codex-unavailable` in the review log, and use internal review findings only for that pass. Do NOT treat a Codex failure as a clean review. Do NOT skip the pass. The next pass still attempts Codex (transient failures may recover).\n   200→\n   201→**Code review scoping by mode:**\n   202→- Use `--uncommitted` when reviewing uncommitted changes (`task-review` mode).\n   203→- Use `--base <sha>` when reviewing committed changes.\n   204→- Use `codex exec -c model=\"$CODEX_MODEL\"` with stdin pipe for non-code artifacts (`spec-challenge`, `design-review`, `plan-review`, `research-review`, `clarification-review` modes).\n   205→- See `docs/reference/review-loop-pattern.md` for code review scoping rules.\n   206→\n   207→#### Gemini Review\n   208→\n   209→If `gemini` is in `multi_tool.tools`, follow the same pattern using the Gemini CLI when available. **For detailed Gemini CLI usage, see `wz:gemini-cli` skill.**\n   210→\n   211→### Fix Cycle (Codex Findings)\n   212→\n   213→If Codex produces blocking findings:\n   214→1. Executor fixes the Codex findings\n   215→2. Re-run internal review (quick pass) to verify fixes didn't introduce regressions\n   216→3. Optionally re-run Codex for a clean pass\n   217→\n   218→### Merging Findings\n   219→\n   220→The final review report must clearly attribute each finding:\n   221→- `[Internal]` — found by Tier 1 internal review\n   222→- `[Codex]` — found by Tier 2 Codex review\n   223→- `[Gemini]` — found by Tier 2 Gemini review\n   224→- `[Both]` — found independently by multiple sources\n   225→\n   226→### Finding Persistence (Learning Pipeline)\n   227→\n   228→ALL findings from both tiers are persisted to `state.sqlite` for cross-run learning:\n   229→\n   230→```javascript\n   231→// After each review pass\n   232→const { insertFinding, getRecurringFindingHashes } = require('tooling/src/state/db');\n   233→const db = openStateDb(stateRoot);\n   234→\n   235→for (const finding of allFindings) {\n   236→  insertFinding(db, {\n   237→    run_id: runId,\n   238→    phase: reviewMode,\n   239→    source: finding.attribution, // 'internal', 'codex', 'gemini'\n   240→    severity: finding.severity,\n   241→    description: finding.description,\n   242→    finding_hash: hashFinding(finding.description),\n   243→  });\n   244→}\n   245→\n   246→// Check for recurring patterns\n   247→const recurring = getRecurringFindingHashes(db, 2);\n   248→// Recurring findings → auto-propose as learnings in the learn phase\n   249→```\n   250→\n   251→This is how Wazir evolves — findings that recur across runs become accepted learnings injected into future executor context, preventing the same mistakes.\n   252→\n   253→## Interaction Mode Awareness\n   254→\n   255→Read `interaction_mode` from run-config:\n   256→\n   257→- **`auto`:** No user checkpoints. Present verdict and let gating agent decide. On escalation, write reason and STOP.\n   258→- **`guided`:** Standard behavior — present verdict, ask user how to proceed.\n   259→- **`interactive`:** Discuss findings with user: \"I found a potential auth bypass in `src/auth.js:42` — here's why I rated it high severity. Do you agree, or is there context I'm missing?\" Show detailed reasoning for each dimension score.\n   260→\n   261→## CLI/Context-Mode Enforcement\n   262→\n   263→In ALL review modes, check for these violations:\n   264→\n   265→1. **Index usage enforcement:** If the agent performed >5 direct file reads (Read tool) without a preceding `wazir index search-symbols` query, flag as **[warning]** finding: \"Agent performed [N] direct file reads without using wazir index. Use `wazir index search-symbols <query>` before reading files to reduce context consumption.\"\n   266→\n   267→2. **Context-mode enforcement:** If the agent ran a large-category command (test runners, builds, diffs, dependency trees, linting — as classified by `hooks/routing-matrix.json`) using native Bash instead of context-mode tools (when context-mode is available), flag as **[warning]** finding: \"Large command `[cmd]` run without context-mode. Route through `mcp__plugin_context-mode_context-mode__execute` to reduce context usage.\"\n   268→\n   269→These are warnings, not blocking findings — they improve efficiency but don't affect correctness.\n   270→\n   271→## Task-Review Log Filenames\n   272→\n   273→In `task-review` mode, use task-scoped log filenames and cap tracking:\n   274→- Log filenames: `.wazir/runs/latest/reviews/execute-task-<NNN>-review-pass-<N>.md`\n   275→- Cap tracking: `wazir capture loop-check --task-id <NNN>` (each task has its own independent cap counter)\n   276→\n   277→## Output\n   278→\n   279→Save review results to `.wazir/runs/latest/reviews/review.md` with:\n   280→- Findings with severity (blocking, warning, note)\n   281→- Rationale tied to evidence\n   282→- Score breakdown\n   283→- Verdict\n   284→\n   285→Run the phase report and display it to the user:\n   286→```bash\n   287→wazir report phase --run <run-id> --phase <review-mode>\n   288→```\n   289→\n   290→Output the report content to the user in the conversation.\n   291→\n   292→## Phase Report Generation\n   293→\n   294→After completing any review pass, generate a phase report following `schemas/phase-report.schema.json`:\n   295→\n   296→1. **`attempted_actions`** — Populate from the review findings. Each finding becomes an action entry:\n   297→   - `description`: the finding summary\n   298→   - `outcome`: `\"success\"` if the finding passed, `\"fail\"` if it is a blocking issue, `\"uncertain\"` if ambiguous\n   299→   - `evidence`: the rationale or evidence supporting the outcome\n   300→\n   301→2. **`drift_analysis`** — Compare review findings against the approved spec:\n   302→   - `delta`: count of deviations between implementation and spec (0 = no drift)\n   303→   - `description`: summary of any drift detected and its impact\n   304→\n   305→3. **`quality_metrics`** — Populate from test, lint, and type-check results gathered during review:\n   306→   - `test_pass_count`, `test_fail_count`: from test runner output\n   307→   - `lint_errors`: from linter output\n   308→   - `type_errors`: from type checker output\n   309→\n   310→4. **`risk_flags`** — Populate from any high-severity findings:\n   311→   - `severity`: `\"low\"`, `\"medium\"`, or `\"high\"`\n   312→   - `description`: what the risk is\n   313→   - `mitigation`: recommended mitigation (if known)\n   314→\n   315→5. **`decisions`** — Populate from any scope or approach decisions made during the review:\n   316→   - `description`: what was decided\n   317→   - `rationale`: why\n   318→   - `alternatives_considered`: other options evaluated (optional)\n   319→   - `source`: `\"[Wazir]\"`, `\"[Codex]\"`, or `\"[Both]\"` (optional)\n   320→\n   321→6. **`verdict_recommendation`** — Set based on the gating rules in `config/gating-rules.yaml`:\n   322→   - `verdict`: `\"continue\"` (PASS), `\"loop_back\"` (NEEDS MINOR FIXES / NEEDS REWORK), or `\"escalate\"` (FAIL with fundamental issues)\n   323→   - `reasoning`: brief explanation of why this verdict was chosen\n   324→\n   325→### Report Output Paths\n   326→\n   327→Save reports to two formats under the run directory:\n   328→- `.wazir/runs/<id>/reports/phase-<name>-report.json` — machine-readable, validated against `schemas/phase-report.schema.json`\n   329→- `.wazir/runs/<id>/reports/phase-<name>-report.md` — human-readable Markdown summary\n   330→\n   331→The gating agent (`tooling/src/gating/agent.js`) consumes the JSON report to decide: **continue**, **loop_back**, or **escalate**.\n   332→\n   333→### Report Fields Reference\n   334→\n   335→All required fields per {"parentUuid":"8186e967-2716-47f8-ad19-d0906c98a9f8","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"262873c7-62f8-4bdd-a59b-56fbe948f330","agentId":"adc2b12a4da32c962","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01RhU9pxU5xksHHT94GiHybC","type":"tool_result","content":"---\ntitle: Reasoning\ndescription: \"Learn how to enable and use agent reasoning to improve task execution.\"\nicon: brain\nmode: \"wide\"\n---\n\n## Overview\n\nAgent reasoning is a feature that allows agents to reflect on a task and create a plan before execution. This helps agents approach tasks more methodically and ensures they're ready to perform the assigned work.\n\n## Usage\n\nTo enable reasoning for an agent, simply set `reasoning=True` when creating the agent:\n\n```python\nfrom crewai import Agent\n\nagent = Agent(\n    role=\"Data Analyst\",\n    goal=\"Analyze complex datasets and provide insights\",\n    backstory=\"You are an experienced data analyst with expertise in finding patterns in complex data.\",\n    reasoning=True,  # Enable reasoning\n    max_reasoning_attempts=3  # Optional: Set a maximum number of reasoning attempts\n)\n```\n\n## How It Works\n\nWhen reasoning is enabled, before executing a task, the agent will:\n\n1. Reflect on the task and create a detailed plan\n2. Evaluate whether it's ready to execute the task\n3. Refine the plan as necessary until it's ready or max_reasoning_attempts is reached\n4. Inject the reasoning plan into the task description before execution\n\nThis process helps the agent break down complex tasks into manageable steps and identify potential challenges before starting.\n\n## Configuration Options\n\n<ParamField body=\"reasoning\" type=\"bool\" default=\"False\"> \n    Enable or disable reasoning \n</ParamField>\n\n<ParamField body=\"max_reasoning_attempts\" type=\"int\" default=\"None\"> \n    Maximum number of attempts to refine the plan before proceeding with execution. If None (default), the agent will continue refining until it's ready. \n</ParamField>\n\n## Example\n\nHere's a complete example:\n\n```python\nfrom crewai import Agent, Task, Crew\n\n# Create an agent with reasoning enabled\nanalyst = Agent(\n    role=\"Data Analyst\",\n    goal=\"Analyze data and provide insights\",\n    backstory=\"You are an expert data analyst.\",\n    reasoning=True,\n    max_reasoning_attempts=3  # Optional: Set a limit on reasoning attempts\n)\n\n# Create a task\nanalysis_task = Task(\n    description=\"Analyze the provided sales data and identify key trends.\",\n    expected_output=\"A report highlighting the top 3 sales trends.\",\n    agent=analyst\n)\n\n# Create a crew and run the task\ncrew = Crew(agents=[analyst], tasks=[analysis_task])\nresult = crew.kickoff()\n\nprint(result)\n```\n\n## Error Handling\n\nThe reasoning process is designed to be robust, with error handling built in. If an error occurs during reasoning, the agent will proceed with executing the task without the reasoning plan. This ensures that tasks can still be executed even if the reasoning process fails.\n\nHere's how to handle potential errors in your code:\n\n```python\nfrom crewai import Agent, Task\nimport logging\n\n# Set up logging to capture any reasoning errors\nlogging.basicConfig(level=logging.INFO)\n\n# Create an agent with reasoning enabled\nagent = Agent(\n    role=\"Data Analyst\",\n    goal=\"Analyze data and provide insights\",\n    reasoning=True,\n    max_reasoning_attempts=3\n)\n\n# Create a task\ntask = Task(\n    description=\"Analyze the provided sales data and identify key trends.\",\n    expected_output=\"A report highlighting the top 3 sales trends.\",\n    agent=agent\n)\n\n# Execute the task\n# If an error occurs during reasoning, it will be logged and execution will continue\nresult = agent.execute_task(task)\n```\n\n## Example Reasoning Output\n\nHere's an example of what a reasoning plan might look like for a data analysis task:\n\n```\nTask: Analyze the provided sales data and identify key trends.\n\nReasoning Plan:\nI'll analyze the sales data to identify the top 3 trends.\n\n1. Understanding of the task:\n   I need to analyze sales data to identify key trends that would be valuable for business decision-making.\n\n2. Key steps I'll take:\n   - First, I'll examine the data structure to understand what fields are available\n   - Then I'll perform exploratory data analysis to identify patterns\n   - Next, I'll analyze sales by time periods to identify temporal trends\n   - I'll also analyze sales by product categories and customer segments\n   - Finally, I'll identify the top 3 most significant trends\n\n3. Approach to challenges:\n   - If the data has missing values, I'll decide whether to fill or filter them\n   - If the data has outliers, I'll investigate whether they're valid data points or errors\n   - If trends aren't immediately obvious, I'll apply statistical methods to uncover patterns\n\n4.   \"\"\"\n        try:\n            # Try task tools first, then agent tools\n            tools = []\n            if self.task:\n                tools = self.task.tools or []\n            if not Let me compile the findings.\n\n---\n\nHere is the complete research output.\n\n## 1. Ideation Team Skill (bladnman) -- Depth System\n\nThe most fully parameterized depth system I found. Four levels: **Quick, Standard, Deep, Exhaustive**. The key insight is that every parameter is a **concrete number injected directly into agent prompts** via a `## Depth Directives for This Session` section appended to each agent's spawn prompt.\n\n### Complete Parameter Table\n\n| Parameter | Quick | Standard | Deep | Exhaustive |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| Min reports before convergence check | 1 | 3 | 5 | 8 |\n| Max reports before forced convergence check | 3 | 6 | 12 | No limit |\n| \"Interesting\" threshold (of 4 criteria) | 1 of 4 | 2 of 4 | 3 of 4 | All 4 |\n| \"Needs more conversation\" tendency | Rare | Moderate | Frequent | Very frequent |\n| Divergence width (directions explored) | 2-3 | 3-5 | 5-8 | 8+ |\n| Exchanges per direction | 3-5 | 5-8 | 8-12 | No limit |\n| Research depth | Only if explicitly requested | On-demand | Parallel with thinkers | Pre-session + parallel |\n| Writer snapshot frequency | 1-2 | 3-5 | 5-8 | 8+ |\n| Time estimate | ~15-30 min | ~45-90 min | ~2-3 hrs | ~3+ hrs |\n\n### How Injected into Agent Prompts\n\nEach agent (Free Thinker, Grounder, Writer, Arbiter) receives a **different directive** for each depth level -- not just a number, but behavioral instructions. For example, the Free Thinker at Quick gets: *\"Explore 2-3 directions maximum. Spend no more than 3-5 exchanges per direction. Favor breadth over depth.\"* At Deep: *\"Explore 5-8 directions. Spend 8-12 exchanges. Push ideas further than feels comfortable. Expect to revisit and deepen ideas multiple times.\"*\n\nThe config is stored in `session-config.yaml` with `depth.level`, `depth.max_rounds`, and `depth.confidence_threshold` fields. The Arbiter reads this config and composes the depth directives before spawning each teammate.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Wazir's Current Depth System\n\nThree levels: **Quick, Standard, Deep**. Currently, depth controls exactly **two things**:\n\n### What Changes Per Level Today\n\n| Parameter | Quick | Standard | Deep |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| Review pass count | 3 | 5 | 7 |\n| Dimension subset | First 3 dims | First 5 dims | All available dims |\n\nThat is the entire depth system. Both are defined in `docs/reference/review-loop-pattern.md`:\n- `pass_counts = { quick: 3, standard: 5, deep: 7 }`\n- `depth_dimensions = { quick: dimensions[0:3], standard: dimensions[0:5], deep: dimensions }`\n- Final review is always 9 dims, 1 pass regardless of depth.\n\n**What does NOT change per depth today:**\n- Research source count (no depth scaling)\n- Question batch size (fixed at 1-3 batches of 3-7 questions)\n- Test coverage threshold (none defined)\n- Proof collection rigor (same for all depths)\n- Model routing (depth-independent; based on task type only)\n- Verification steps (same for all depths)\n- Loop cap (operator-configured, independent of depth)\n\nThe depth is set via inline modifiers (`/wazir quick ...`, `/wazir deep ...`) and defaults to `standard`. It is parsed by `tooling/src/init/auto-detect.js` and stored in the run config.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Devin's Approach to Task Complexity\n\nDevin (from Cognition) uses a **binary mode system**, not depth levels:\n\n- **\"Planning\" mode**: The agent gathers information, searches the codebase, uses the browser for research. It calls `<suggest_plan/>` when ready. No implementation happens in this mode.\n- **\"Standard\" mode**: The agent executes plan steps. It sees current and possible next steps and outputs actions.\n\nThere is **no depth/thoroughness parameter**. The system routes externally -- the orchestrator (not the agent) decides when to switch modes. There is no public evidence of a complexity-based routing system. Devin's approach is: plan fully before executing, rather than scaling the planning depth.\n\nKey Devin design: `<think>` command for internal reasoning scratchpad (invisible to user), `<semantic_search>` for codebase understanding, and parallel multi-command output.\n\n---\n\n## 4. CrewAI's Task Complexity / Priority Systems\n\nCrewAI has **no explicit depth/thoroughness level system**. Instead, it provides several granular knobs that can be composed:\n\n| Mechanism | What it controls | Default |\n|---|---|---|\n| `max_iter` (per agent) | Maximum iterations for task execution | 25 |\n| `max_reasoning_attempts` (per agent) | Pre-task planning refinement loops | None (unlimited until ready) |\n| `reasoning=True/False` (per agent) | Whether agent plans before executing | False |\n| `guardrail` (per task) | Output validation (function or LLM-based) | None |\n| `guardrail_max_retries` (per task) | Retry count when guardrail fails | 3 |\n| `planning=True/False` (per crew) | Whether the crew plans before kickoff | False |\n| `planning_llm` (per crew) | Which model plans for the crew | Agent's own LLM |\n| `verbose` | Logging verbosity | False |\n\nCrewAI's **LLM Selection Guide** provides a complexity framework (not automated):\n- **Simple tasks**: basic instruction following, clear I/O -- cheap models\n- **Complex tasks**: multi-step reasoning, ambiguity handling -- capable models  \n- **Creative tasks**: novel generation, tone awareness -- creative models\n\nThe model selection is manual per-agent, not depth-driven. The `reasoning_handler.py` iterates `create_plan -> refine_plan` until `ready=True` or `max_attempts` hit, similar in spirit to Wazir's review loop but without fixed pass counts.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Superpowers Framework\n\nSuperpowers has **no depth level system**. It uses fixed review iteration caps:\n\n- Spec review loop: max **3 iterations** then escalate to human\n- Plan review loop: max **3 iterations** then escalate to human\n- Code review: **2-stage** (spec compliance, then code quality), loop until approved\n\nTask complexity routing is done by **model selection per task type**:\n- Touches 1-2 files with complete spec -> cheap model\n- Multiple files with integration concerns -> standard model\n- Design judgment or broad codebase understanding -> most capable model\n\nThis is not parameterized by a depth level -- it's a per-task heuristic.\n\n---\n\n## 6.
